## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillator dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where dv_dt is determined by restoring forces (functions of x), damping forces (functions of v), and possibly external driving forces (functions of t). Classical nonlinear oscillator models like Duffing, van der Pol, and Mathieu equations apply.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Duffing with damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (externally driven nonlinear oscillator)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * cos(c1 * t) + c2 * v (time-modulated stiffness)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * x**2 + c2 * v (position-dependent damping)
- Cubic damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v**3 + c2 * v (velocity-cubic dissipation)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (Rayleigh-type nonlinear damping)
- Softening/hardening spring with drive: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * sin(c4 * t + c5) (general driven Duffing)
- Mixed nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v (asymmetric restoring force with damping)
- Mathieu-Duffing: dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x + c3 * x**3 + c4 * v (parametric + nonlinear)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) → symmetric potential wells preserving oscillator symmetry
- Even-power position terms (x²) → asymmetric potential indicating broken symmetry in the restoring force
- Velocity multiplied by position-dependent factor (v*(1 - x²)) → amplitude-dependent damping characteristic of self-sustained oscillators like van der Pol
- Product of position and trigonometric function of time (x*cos(c*t)) → parametric excitation where stiffness is modulated periodically
- Additive sinusoidal time dependence (sin(c*t)) → external periodic driving force independent of system state
- Cubic velocity terms (v³) → nonlinear dissipation that becomes dominant at high velocities
- Absence of explicit time dependence → autonomous system where phase portrait analysis applies and energy is conserved or monotonically changing
- Cross terms like x*v → coupling between position and velocity suggesting non-conservative or gyroscopic-like forces
